## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting mechanical stress as a function of strain and temperature, which is a classic problem in solid mechanics and materials science. The relationship captures how materials deform under load and how temperature affects mechanical properties such as elastic modulus, yield strength, and flow stress.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)

- {'name': 'Exponential thermal softening', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T)', 'scenario': 'Elastic or flow stress with Arrhenius-type thermal dependence'}
- {'name': 'Voce hardening law', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon)', 'scenario': 'Saturation-type strain hardening approaching a limiting stress'}
- {'name': 'Voce with thermal dependence', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - c2 * exp(c3 * epsilon))', 'scenario': 'Saturation hardening with temperature-dependent saturation stress'}
- {'name': 'Ludwik equation', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2', 'scenario': 'Yield stress plus power-law hardening'}
- {'name': 'Swift hardening law', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2', 'scenario': 'Power-law hardening with pre-strain offset'}
- {'name': 'Linear modulus with temperature', 'formula': 'sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon', 'scenario': "Linear elastic with linearly temperature-dependent Young's modulus"}
- {'name': 'Polynomial stress-strain-temperature', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * T * epsilon', 'scenario': 'Second-order expansion in strain with strain-temperature coupling'}
- {'name': 'Hyperbolic sine creep law (Garofalo)', 'formula': 'sigma = c0 * T * sinh(c1 * epsilon)', 'scenario': 'High-temperature creep and viscoplastic flow'}

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent modulus → Multiplicative factor (c0 + c1*T) or exp(c2*T) scaling the stress-strain relationship
- Strain hardening saturation → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), or rational form epsilon/(epsilon + c)
- Thermal softening → Stress multiplied by decreasing function of T: (1 - c*(T/Tm)**n), exp(-c*T), or (Tm - T)**c
- Nonlinear elasticity → Odd-power polynomial in strain: c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**3, reflecting symmetric tension-compression
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T or epsilon**c1 * T**c2 indicating interactive thermo-mechanical effects
- Yield point offset → Additive constant c0 representing initial yield stress before hardening: sigma = c0 + f(epsilon)
- Phase transition or softening discontinuity → Sigmoidal temperature dependence: tanh(c0*(T - c1)) modulating stress level
- Rubber/hyperelastic behavior → Polynomial or inverse power terms in strain: c0*(epsilon - c1*epsilon**(-2)) for large deformation

**GT:** `64.95*epsilon**0.614*exp(-36.95/(8.314*T)) - 0.215*(T - 331.68) + 3.554*(T - 331.68)*log(epsilon + 1)`

Let me expand the GT:
- Term 1: `c0*epsilon**c1*exp(-c2/(c3*T))` — involves both epsilon and T through an exponential Arrhenius-like term
- Term 2: `-c4*(T - c5)` = `-c4*T + c4*c5` — linear in T
- Term 3: `c6*(T - c7)*log(epsilon + 1)` = `c6*T*log(epsilon+1) - c6*c7*log(epsilon+1)` — involves T*log(epsilon+1) and log(epsilon+1)

The key structural features of GT:
1. `epsilon**c1 * exp(-const/T)` — power of epsilon times Arrhenius in T
2. Linear term in T (constant w.r.t. epsilon)
3. `T * log(epsilon + 1)` — product of T and log(epsilon+1)
4. `log(epsilon + 1)` — standalone
5. Constant term

The critical basis functions involving T are: `exp(-const/T)`, `T`, and `T*log(epsilon+1)`. Any candidate must be able to reproduce these T-dependencies.

Let me check each candidate for the presence of these essential T-dependent structures:

**Candidates without T dependence (1, 3, 4, 8, 10, 16, 17, 18, 26, 41, 43, 51, 57):** These cannot match GT since GT has explicit T dependence that cannot be zeroed out without losing essential terms. → **NO MATCH** for all.

**Candidates with only `T*epsilon` type T-dependence (5, 9, 19, 22, 28, 30, 32, 37, 44, 47, 53, 55, 59, 61, 65):** These have T appearing as `T*epsilon` or `sqrt(T+c)` or `(epsilon+c)^(1/3)`, but NOT `T*log(epsilon+1)` or `exp(-c/T)`. The GT requires `T*log(epsilon+1)` which cannot be produced from `T*epsilon`. → **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with `T*epsilon` and `log(T*c+1)` (6, 12, 13, 14, 36, 46, 60, 62, 63):** `log(T*c+1)` is NOT equivalent to T (it's a nonlinear function of T). The GT needs `T*log(epsilon+1)` but these have `epsilon*log(T*c+1)` which is structurally different. → **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with `log(c*exp(T*c)+1)` (2, 39):** `log(c8*exp(T*c9)+1)` ≈ for large argument becomes linear in T, but this is an approximation, not exact equivalence. → **NO MATCH**.
